**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is May, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

Breaking political news

Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

Most notably, the CDC's infection control committee has been shut down [18], potentially affecting public health monitoring capabilities. The administration is also restructuring the U.S. Postal Service, with Trump urging the USPS board to appoint a FedEx official as postmaster general [6], while some reporting suggests this may be part of a broader privatization effort that could benefit Amazon [12]. The National Security Agency faces significant staffing reductions, with plans to cut 2,000 civilian roles by year's end [36]. Additionally, the Drug Enforcement Administration is abandoning body cameras [63] despite previously promoting them for transparency purposes. Worker safety has also been affected, with the dismantling of a key worker safety group characterized as harmful to working-class interests [76]. The Department of Justice did announce results of a drug bust involving Attorney General Pamela Bondi, the DEA, and the U.S. Attorney's Office for New Mexico [27]. The Veterans Administration is reportedly implementing job cuts, which VA leadership claims will improve efficiency [19].

The Trump administration has made several significant policy shifts in the Middle East. Topic 2.5: U.S.-Canada Relations (importance: 5)
U.S.-Canada relations have become notably strained under the Trump administration, as evidenced by several confrontational exchanges. During an Oval Office meeting, Canadian Prime Minister Mark Carney firmly stated that "Canada is not for sale, ever," to which President Trump responded, "never say never" [30]. This exchange suggests tension over potential American economic interests in Canadian assets or resources. The meeting also included Trump praising Carney as a "very good person" despite their differences [8]. A fact check by CNN contradicted Trump's claim that the U.S. doesn't do "much business with Canada," noting that Canada is actually the top buyer of U.S. exports [17]. The strain in bilateral relations appears to be affecting travel patterns, with WestJet suspending nine U.S. routes as "Canadians avoid America" [4]. In the context of preparations for the 2026 World Cup, which Canada will co-host with the U.S. and Mexico, Trump has attempted to downplay tensions, claiming there's "no tension" between the countries [44]. However, Commerce Secretary Lutnick has expressed skepticism about cutting deals with what he characterized as Canada's "socialist regime" [21].

These actions represent municipal-level resistance to state policies limiting LGBTQ+ expression or representation, highlighting growing tension between different levels of government on civil rights issues. # DAILY BRIEFING: MAY 2025

## 1. EXECUTIVE ACTIONS & GOVERNANCE

### 1.1 Administrative Restructuring & DOGE
The Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), headed by Elon Musk, has initiated plans to consolidate federal data, raising significant privacy concerns. According to the Washington Post, this data pooling effort could put Americans' personal information at risk [1].

### 1.2 Federal Agency Changes
The Trump administration has implemented sweeping changes across multiple federal agencies. The CDC's infection control committee has been shut down [2], potentially affecting public health monitoring capabilities. The administration is restructuring the U.S. Postal Service, with Trump urging the USPS board to appoint a FedEx official as postmaster general [3], while some reporting suggests this may be part of a broader privatization effort [4]. 

The National Security Agency faces significant staffing reductions, with plans to cut 2,000 civilian roles by year's end [5]. The Drug Enforcement Administration is abandoning body cameras [6] despite previously promoting them for transparency. Worker safety has also been affected, with the dismantling of a key worker safety group [7]. The Veterans Administration is reportedly implementing job cuts, which VA leadership claims will improve efficiency [8].

### 1.3 Legal Challenges
The administration faces mounting legal challenges. The Supreme Court allowed Trump's transgender military ban to take effect [9], representing a victory for the administration's military personnel policies. However, judges have temporarily blocked the dismantling of the library services agency [10] and three other unspecified agencies [11]. The administration also experienced a legal defeat in a dispute with law firm Perkins Coie [12]. Hawaii appears to be pursuing multiple legal actions against the White House, as evidenced by tracking efforts of these cases [13].

### 1.4 Appointments & Nominations
Presidential appointments reveal both successes and challenges. Key Republican Senator Thom Tillis has opposed Trump loyalist Ed Martin's nomination as U.S. attorney for Washington D.C., likely derailing the appointment [14]. The Senate confirmed Trump's pick, Bisignano, to lead the Social Security Administration [15]. Attorney General Pamela Bondi has been involved in a major drug bust alongside the DEA and U.S. Attorney's Office for New Mexico [16], while Trump has selected Rudy Giuliani's son for a key World Cup post [17].

## 2. FOREIGN POLICY & INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS

### 2.1 Middle East Policies
The Trump administration has made several significant policy shifts in the Middle East. President Trump has stated that "less than 2 dozen hostages" are believed to be alive in Gaza [1]. He has announced that the U.S. will stop bombing Houthi militants [2], citing a truce with the Houthis after they promised to cease targeting ships [3]. In a separate development with potential diplomatic implications, the administration plans to rename the Persian Gulf as the "Arabian Gulf" [4], widely interpreted as a deliberate snub to Iran.

### 2.2 Global Conflicts & Diplomacy
The administration faces criticism for its approach to two major international conflicts. President Trump has described Indian strikes in the Kashmir dispute as a "shame" [5], while questions emerge about whether he will help India and Pakistan "pull back from brink of war" [6]. Meanwhile, former President Biden has launched pointed criticism of Trump's Ukraine policy, characterizing Trump's pressure on Ukraine as "modern-day appeasement" toward Russia [7].

U.S.-China relations appear to be entering a tentative diplomatic phase with plans for an "ice-breaker meeting" between officials from both countries scheduled in Geneva [8].

### 2.3 U.S.-Canada Relations
U.S.-Canada relations have become notably strained. During an Oval Office meeting, Canadian Prime Minister Mark Carney firmly stated that "Canada is not for sale, ever," to which President Trump responded, "never say never" [1]. The meeting also highlighted "gaping differences" on tariffs and the potential admission of a 51st state [2]. A fact check contradicted Trump's claim that the U.S. doesn't do "much business with Canada," noting that Canada is actually the top buyer of U.S. exports [3]. The strain in relations appears to be affecting travel patterns, with WestJet suspending nine U.S. routes as "Canadians avoid America" [4].

## 3. CONGRESSIONAL & LEGISLATIVE AFFAIRS

### 3.1 Congressional Investigations
Congressional oversight activities are targeting both the administration and judicial processes. Senator Elizabeth Warren is pushing for an investigation into a cryptocurrency deal involving the Trump family [1], which may be related to Senate Democrats' proposed "ban on presidents investing or endorsing crypto assets" [2]. Senate Judiciary Committee Chairman Dick Durbin has requested a Department of Justice investigation into anonymous pizza deliveries to judges [3]. Congressional Democrats, led by Senator Bernie Sanders, are urging Paramount not to settle what they characterize as a "shakedown" lawsuit involving CBS [4].

### 3.2 Electoral Politics & Legislation
The political landscape is shifting ahead of upcoming elections. Robert F. Kennedy Jr. is navigating the challenges of implementing his food policy agenda amid the "realities of governing" [1]. In Georgia, Republicans are searching for a "backup plan" in the Senate race [2], complicated by Governor Brian Kemp's decision to reject a Senate run [3]. In New York City, former Governor Andrew Cuomo has announced plans to run for mayor as both "an independent and a Democrat" [4].

A Republican effort to formalize President Trump's "Gulf of America" renaming has encountered resistance in the House [5]. The House has introduced bills targeting economic and environmental policies, including legislation to create Universal Savings Accounts [6] and to amend the Clean Air Act regarding locomotive emissions standards [7].

## 4. ECONOMIC & TRADE POLICY

### 4.1 Tariff Implementation & Trade Deficit
The Trump administration's tariff policies coincide with a growing U.S. trade deficit. Recent data shows the trade deficit expanding in the first quarter [1] and hitting a record high ahead of new Trump tariffs [2]. The Federal Reserve now faces what the Wall Street Journal characterizes as a "Lose-Lose Scenario Amid Haphazard Tariff Rollout" [3]. The impact is extending to financial markets, with Trump tariffs and export restrictions on China "casting a cloud over major chip stocks" [4]. President Trump appears uncompromising, with reports that he "Downplays Trade Negotiations, Says He'll Dictate Terms" [5]. Ireland has downgraded its growth prospects "in face of Trump tariffs" [6].

### 4.2 Tax Legislation & Entitlement Programs
Republicans face challenges in advancing tax legislation. A proposed financing mechanism for Trump's tax cuts involves "Sales of Public Land" [1]. The tax legislation faces resistance from within Republican ranks, with "5 blue-state Republicans willing to sink tax bill over state, local deduction" [2]. A tax bill containing "deep Medicaid cuts" is reportedly "imperiled" by vocal Republican critic Representative Don Bacon [3]. The proposed Medicaid changes would "Charge Poor People More for Coverage" [4].

## 5. MILITARY & IMMIGRATION

### 5.1 Military Equipment & Operations
The U.S. Navy has experienced two serious equipment failures involving fighter jets from the Harry S. Truman aircraft carrier. Reports confirm that a "Second US Navy jet is lost at sea" [1] after falling off the carrier. Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth has "twice extended the deployment of the aircraft carrier involved in the losses" [2]. Each jet is valued at approximately $70 million according to reporting, representing a significant loss of military assets.

The Trump administration has directed a shift in intelligence priorities with an order for intelligence agencies to "step up spying on Greenland" [3], though the strategic reasoning behind this directive is not explained in the headline.

### 5.2 Immigration & Border Security

### 2.3 U.S.-Canada Relations
U.S.-Canada relations have become notably strained. A fact check contradicted Trump's claim that the U.S. doesn't do "much business with Canada," noting that Canada is actually the top buyer of U.S. exports [3]. The strain in relations appears to be affecting travel patterns, with WestJet suspending nine U.S. routes as "Canadians avoid America" [4].

The impact is extending to financial markets, with Trump tariffs and export restrictions on China "casting a cloud over major chip stocks" [4]. President Trump appears uncompromising, with reports that he "Downplays Trade Negotiations, Says He'll Dictate Terms" [5]. Ireland has downgraded its growth prospects "in face of Trump tariffs" [6].
